<span id="freeTextContainer15640516583194146198">A <strong>New York Times</strong> bestseller! Lucas Davenport returns in the most harrowing and unexpected Prey novel yet<strong>—</strong>the story of a congenial man, and his most uncongenial obsession...<br /><br />An art history professor and writer and cheerful pervert, James Qatar had a hobby: he took secret photographs of women and turned them into highly sexual drawings. One day, he took the hobby a step furth</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15640516583194146198">A <strong>New York Times</strong> bestseller! Lucas Davenport returns in the most harrowing and unexpected Prey novel yet<strong>—</strong>the story of a congenial man, and his most uncongenial obsession...<br /><br />An art history professor and writer and cheerful pervert, James Qatar had a hobby: he took secret photographs of women and turned them into highly sexual drawings. One day, he took the hobby a step further and... well, one thing led to another, and he had to kill her. A man in his position couldn't be too careful, after all. And you know something? He liked it.<br /><br />Already faced with a welter of confusion in his personal life, Deputy Chief Lucas Davenport decides to take this case himself, hoping that some straightforward police work will clear his head, but as the trail begins to take some unexpected turns, it soon becomes clear that nothing is straightforward about this killer. The man is learning as he goes, Lucas realizes, taking great strides forward with each murder. He is becoming a monster — and Lucas may have no choice but to walk right into his lair...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15640516583194146198">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_6985990">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6985990" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/405390-kemper" class="left imgcol" title="Kemper"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451574879p2/405390.jpg" alt="Kemper" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/6985990?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/405390-kemper" class="user" title="Kemper">Kemper</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery" class="actionLinkLite">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=serial-killers" class="actionLinkLite">serial-killers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=5-0" class="actionLinkLite">5-0</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=lucas-davenport" class="actionLinkLite">lucas-davenport</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2013-reread" class="actionLinkLite">2013-reread</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer6985990">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5706496135199614470">A long Minnesota winter has left Lucas Davenport in one of his funks, but fortunately there’s a hunt for a new serial killer to put a spring in his step and a song in his heart.<br /><br />James Qatar is an art history professor who likes luring lonely women into romances and then strangling them. His other hobby is doing explicit pornographic drawings of females he’s angry with and sending them the pictures anonymously or posting them in a public place. So Qatar is a real peach of a guy.<br /><br />A recently discover</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5706496135199614470">A long Minnesota winter has left Lucas Davenport in one of his funks, but fortunately there’s a hunt for a new serial killer to put a spring in his step and a song in his heart.<br /><br />James Qatar is an art history professor who likes luring lonely women into romances and then strangling them. His other hobby is doing explicit pornographic drawings of females he’s angry with and sending them the pictures anonymously or posting them in a public place. So Qatar is a real peach of a guy.<br /><br />A recently discovered body is linked to complaints about the drawings, and a Wisconsin deputy who has been investigating his missing niece shows up with a pattern of missing women that fits the victim’s profile. Lucas smells a freak and launches a hunt. There’s the usual Sandford cat-and-mouse game with the reader getting Qatar’s psychotic point of view as he engages in increasingly violent efforts to keep from being caught.<br /><br />It’s a good news/bad news scenario for Lucas on the personal side of things in this one. The good news is that he has reconciled with a former girlfriend and things are going so well that they’re considering having a baby. The bad news is that politics are going to force the current police chief out in a few months and Lucas along with her.<br /><br />While the personal angles signal that change is on the horizon for Lucas, the rest of this book seems a bit formulaic and repetitive. Qatar is a decent enough villain, but Sandford had leaned a bit too heavily on the crazy serial killer targeting women already so despite some effort to differentiate him from the others, it still seems overly familiar. Plus, there are other elements that reminded me a lot of <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/630908779">Night Prey</a> like Lucas working with a cop who has a personal obsession with finding the killer and a woman being used as bait at one point.<br /><br />There’s an interesting sub-plot about Lucas having to deal with an old foe to get critical information, and also a nice curve ball thrown in at the end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[I really liked how Lucas figured out that Terry was going to try and kill Qatar, and that he wasn’t sure how to play it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Still, while it’s another entertaining thriller from Sandford, it’s not one of the most memorable books in the <em>Prey</em> series.<br /><br /><strong>Next:</strong> Lucas hunts an old enemy and tries to plan a wedding in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6985980">Mortal Prey.</a> <br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5706496135199614470">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_95408294">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95408294" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane" class="left imgcol" title="James Thane"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442513566p2/3483907.jpg" alt="James Thane" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/95408294?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 26, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane" class="user" title="James Thane">James Thane</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=crime-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=lucas-davenport" class="actionLinkLite">lucas-davenport</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=john-sandford" class="actionLinkLite">john-sandford</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer95408294">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15039510562266795422">The twelfth entry in John Sandford's acclaimed Prey series finds the world of the protagonist, Lucas Davenport, undergoing some major changes. His boss, Police Chief Rose Marie Roux, is about to lose her job since the mayor who appointed her is leaving office. This means, in turn, that Davenport will almost certainly lose <em>his</em> job as Assistant Chief as well. <br /><br />At the same time, Lucas's girlfriend, Weather Karkinnen, has decided that it's time for them to make a baby. Weather has been alienated from</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15039510562266795422">The twelfth entry in John Sandford's acclaimed Prey series finds the world of the protagonist, Lucas Davenport, undergoing some major changes. His boss, Police Chief Rose Marie Roux, is about to lose her job since the mayor who appointed her is leaving office. This means, in turn, that Davenport will almost certainly lose <em>his</em> job as Assistant Chief as well. <br /><br />At the same time, Lucas's girlfriend, Weather Karkinnen, has decided that it's time for them to make a baby. Weather has been alienated from Lucas for a long while because of an incident that occurred at the end of a previous book, but now she's back. This does not mean that Weather has decided that she would like to be engaged to Davenport again, but her biological clock is ticking and she does need <em>someone</em> to father the child...<br /><br />In the midst of all this, a young woman's decomposing body is discovered partially buried on a rural hillside. She's been missing for about a year, and there is virtually no evidence suggesting who her killer might have been. As Davenport attempts to untangle the mystery, a rural Wisconsin marshal appears with a file he's been keeping on missing young women who have disappeared much like Davenport's victim. One of the missing women is the marshal's niece and Lucas suddenly realizes that he may have a serial killer on his hands.<br /><br />He does, of course, and Lucas rallies his usual team and sends them into action. The killer is a professor of art history named James Qatar. (This gives nothing away; as is almost always in the case in these books, the reader meets the killer before Davenport even appears on the scene.) Qatar has some particularly sick fantasies that he is acting out and is capable of some pretty unsettling violence. But he's also unusually clever and lucky, and Davenport will have to draw upon all of his legendary skills if he's going to run Qatar to ground.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book a lot. As always, the banter is great; it's fun to watch Weather mess with Lucas, both mentally and physically; the pace is good, and the payoff at the end is rewarding. If I have any complaint about the book (and it's a small one), it's that I didn't think that James Qatar was in the same league as many of the other antagonists in this series.<br /><br />The quality of these books almost always depends on the quality of the villain as well as that of the hero, Davenport. Sandford is capable of creating some truly nasty and memorable adversaries for Lucas, and to my mind, Qatar is not among the better of them. But then, Sandford did give us a fantastic character in Clara Rinker, who appears in two of the Prey books, and so I'm perfectly happy to forgive him if he can't measure up to that level of perfection every time out of the gate. An easy four stars for this one.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15039510562266795422">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1171811804">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1171811804" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie" class="left imgcol" title="Kathy Davie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" alt="Kathy Davie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1171811804?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie" class="user" title="Kathy Davie">Kathy Davie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/12071030-chosen-prey" title="Hardcover " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1171811804">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14897767198816433295">Twelfth in the Lucas Davenport thriller series and revolving around an unorthodox cop in Minneapolis. It's been a year since <a title="Opens John Sandford's Easy Prey in Goodreads" target="_blank" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6838.Easy_Prey"> <em>Easy Prey</em> </a>, 11.<br /><br /><strong>My Take</strong><br />What I like about this series is that it's standard mystery/thriller reading, but Sandford's characters come out so real. That encounter between Lucas and Jeff Baxter was great. They could be talking about golf or tennis, but they're batting around ideas for a deal for a scumbag that Baxter is representing. There are the political issues when Rose Ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14897767198816433295">Twelfth in the Lucas Davenport thriller series and revolving around an unorthodox cop in Minneapolis. It's been a year since <a title="Opens John Sandford's Easy Prey in Goodreads" target="_blank" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6838.Easy_Prey">
  <em>Easy Prey</em>
</a>, 11.<br /><br /><strong>My Take</strong><br />What I like about this series is that it's standard mystery/thriller reading, but Sandford's characters come out so real. That encounter between Lucas and Jeff Baxter was great. They could be talking about golf or tennis, but they're batting around ideas for a deal for a scumbag that Baxter is representing. There are the political issues when Rose Marie warns Lucas they'll probably lose their jobs with the new mayor coming in; she doesn't think any of the potential appointees would keep him. The media issues as we read how the police are manipulating the press. The cops and how they interact, and Lucas and Weather. <br /><br />Oh, yeah, baby…Lucas <em>and</em> Weather. I gotta say, I can understand Weather having insecurity issues about the women in Lucas' life, but she's the one who left. I dunno, though. I do like Lucas. I like that it's important to him to get the right bad guy. I like that he develops role-playing games. But the boy needs to learn how to make a proposal, lol. This sure ain't what I'd be mooning about or sighing over as I remembered that "magic" moment years later, *more laughter*. It only gets better when you read how Whitcomb decorates his house. Oh. My. God.<br /><br />Poor Ellen. She's had a very disappointing love life, and meeting James Qatar is simply another disappointment. Until she decides to put herself first. Women do need to be more open to saying what they want in bed, although Ellen takes it too far, to her regret.<br /><br />Now, James is like too many men. Thinking they're studs and that if they could just meet the right woman, sigh. He will definitely give you a few laughs. I do wish that he could hear the laughter — I'd love to see the look on his face. There's also his obsession with how good he looks, and then Ellen provides her viewpoint on how beauteous James is, lol. Then it gets even better when Kidd does his assessment of the quality of the artist *see me grinning like a mad fool*.<br /><br />Seriously though, Qatar is a piece of work. I couldn't believe that anyone can be that delusional. <em>Does make me feel better about myself, lol!</em> Some of his self-pitying moments…I wanted to smack him upside the head. With a crowbar. He really believes he's so smart, so talented, so handsome, so put-upon <em>poor baby</em>, then Sandford lets everyone else get their chance to dig away at him and show him up. For all the "whining" he does about his mother's sexual history, there are just a few too many <em>off</em> words that make me doubt most of what he says. Well, and the fact that he is so delusional at the best of times.<br /><br />LOL, good advice from Del:<br /><blockquote>"'It just occurred to me that there've only been two women on the newscast,' Marcy said. "And you've slept with both of them, Lucas. Was Carey better than me, or was I better?'Del looked at Lucas and said, 'Run.'"</blockquote><br />More good advice for the budding serial killer. There's also good advice victims never take: call the cops as soon as you suspect something. Never hang on to it to think or thinking you should mention it to the "bad guy" and get his take on it. I mean, duh…haven't they been doing any reading or watching any movies??<br /><br />And then there are the people who should not be allowed outside the house until they've taken an IQ test, oh brother. And the mothers who should get their kids some HELP!<br /><br />Wow. Kidd's analysis of the photo-porn was impressive as he pointed out all the obvious (once he made me aware of the) markers that will provide a ton more clues. It's simply a matter of applying that artist's eye as opposed to the pervy one.<br /><br />I gotta say, I can't believe the cops didn't think about protecting Ellen.<br /><br />Omigod, I thought as Lucas did, and then Weather finishes out her thought. I'm definitely with her. It's a righteous ending. It's also the saddest ending, and I cried.<br /><br /><em>Chosen Prey</em> is a rather shocking mix of horrific and hilarious. What Qatar does, how he thinks will make you wonder what's wrong with our world that someone like him can go undetected for so long, and then more real life inserts itself with that snark that helps cops cope with what they see. And yes, I'm prejudiced. I enjoy that snark, lol.<br /><br /><strong>The Story</strong><br />The grave was too shallow and those autumn rains reveal her to a hunter. It's just the start of what they'll find. But not before he kills again.<br /><br /><strong>The Characters</strong><br /><strong>Deputy Chief Lucas Davenport</strong> is a cop who gets the job done all while keeping the press happy. He's friends with Julie Aronson's parents, <strong>Dolly</strong> and her husband. <strong>Weather Karkinnen</strong> is a surgeon who was once engaged to Lucas until events in <a title="Opens John Sandford's https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/168569.Sudden_Prey in Goodreads" target="_blank" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/168569.Sudden_Prey">
  <em>Sudden Prey</em>
</a>, 8, a couple years ago. <strong>Catrin</strong> (the "Photo Queen") is an old college girlfriend whose marriage broke up; she and Lucas are friends. Still.<br /><br /><em>Minneapolis PD</em><br />Lucas has formed his <strong>Strategic Studies and Planning Group</strong>, and it includes <strong>Del Capslock</strong>, an undercover cop (<strong>Cheryl</strong> is his wife); <strong>Lane</strong>; and, <strong>Tom Black</strong>, Marcy's former partner will join them temporarily. Homicide includes <strong>Marcy Sherrill</strong> (Weather calls her "Titsy"; Marcy is desperate to get back to work even though she's still recovering from injuries in <a title="Opens John Sandford's Easy Prey in Goodreads" target="_blank" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6838.Easy_Prey">
  <em>Easy Prey</em>
</a>). <strong> Detective Swanson</strong> prefers the nightshift. Other cops helping are <strong>McGrady</strong>, <strong>Gibson</strong>, and <strong>Barnes</strong>. <strong>Detective Sloan</strong> is one of Lucas' best friends. <strong>Harmon Anderson</strong> is their computer geek. <strong>Greg Webster</strong> and <strong>Sandy MacMillan</strong> are crime-scene specialists. <strong>Craig Bowden</strong> and <strong>Marc White</strong> are assigned to follow Qatar. <strong>Carolyn Rie</strong> is a detective with sex crimes. <strong>Deputy Chief of Investigations Frank Lester</strong> supervises all investigative units. <strong>Rose Marie Roux</strong> is the chief of police. <strong>Randall Towson</strong> is the county attorney; <strong>Donald Dunn</strong> is his chief deputy; and, Richard Kirk is head of the criminal division. <strong>Larsen</strong> is an assistant county attorney. <strong>Harry Page</strong> is at the Ramsey Public Defender's Office. <strong>Rob Lansing</strong> is the officious little prick more interested in status games. <strong>J.B. Glass</strong> is another defense attorney.<br /><br /><em>St. Paul PD</em><br /><strong>John Davis</strong> is a patrol sergeant, and <strong>Lieutenant Allport</strong>.<br /><br /><em>Goodhue County PD</em><br /><strong>Carl Boone</strong> is the medical examiner.<br /><br /><em>South Dakota County PD</em><br /><strong>Don Hammond </strong>is its chief deputy. <strong>Rick</strong> and <strong>Dave</strong> are part of his team.<br /><br /><em>Ramsay County PD</em><br /><strong>Flanagan</strong> is an investigator who dealt with the bridge death.<br /><br /><em>Dunn County PD in Wisconsin</em><br /><strong>Sheriff Deputy Terry Marshall</strong> is hot on the case of his missing niece, <strong>Laura Winton</strong>.<br /><br /><em>FBI</em><br /><strong>Mallard</strong> is an FBI agent Lucas knows who is based in Washington D.C. <strong>Baily</strong> is the agent-in-charge in Minneapolis.<br /><em>The Media</em><br />Channel 3's <strong>Jennifer Carey</strong> is the mother of Lucas' only child, <strong>Sarah</strong>, who lives with Carey and her husband.<br /><br /><em>St. Patrick's University</em><br /><strong>James Qatar</strong> is an art history professor, writer, and killer with an ego bigger than a Boeing jet. <strong>Helen Qatar</strong> is his mother and the director for the Wells Museum at the college. <em>For such a smart woman, she's pretty stupid.</em> <strong>Denise Thompson</strong> is her very observant secretary. <strong>Burns Goodwin</strong> is the college president. <strong>Charlotte Neumann</strong> is the art department's chairperson, an ordained Episcopalian priest, and a writer. <strong>Elene</strong> is the inept department secretary.<br /><br /><strong>Kidd</strong> is an artist doing really well who lends a hand (to the cops) and a good bit more (to Marcy). <strong>Larry Lake</strong> is an engineering consultant with ground-penetrating radar. <strong>Megan Earle</strong> is a neighbor of Whitcomb's. <strong>George</strong> is one of the people at Christmas Ink, and he doesn't want to say anything, see anything.<br /><br /><em>The film warehouse is…</em><br />…where videos are shot; Morris likes to photograph little girls having sex. <strong>Donald Henrey </strong>has a <em>big</em> camera while <strong>Anthony Carr </strong>maintains his website. <strong>Sylvia Berne</strong> is some of the talent. <strong>Jeff Baxter</strong> is a lawyer.<br /><br /><em>Victims</em><br /><strong>Ellen Barstad</strong> is a fabric artist and a teacher with her own quilting business. <strong>Emily Patton</strong> recognized one victim. <strong>Beverly Wood</strong> is one of the women who got a nude drawing of herself. <strong>Linda Kyle</strong> is an art student who disappeared. <strong>Nancy Vanderpost</strong> disappeared, a performance artist. <strong>Jim Wise</strong> is one of the partners in Wise-Hammersmith American Loft furniture who needed some ads. <strong>Brenda</strong> is from Lino Lakes. <strong>Ellice Hampton</strong> is from Clear Lake, Iowa, and she did advertising layouts.<br /><br /><strong>Tom Lang</strong> is a possible suspect in the serial killings. <strong>Harold Brown</strong> hired Langhorn to find <strong>Lynette Brown</strong>'s body, although he is a high-priority suspect in her disappearance. Into egg cartons. <strong>Randy Whitcomb</strong> is a jerk of a pimp we first met in <a title="Opens John Sandford's Eyes of Prey in Goodreads" target="_blank" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37297.Eyes_of_Prey">
  <em>Eyes of Prey</em>
</a>, 3, and has been Qatar's fence and drug dealer. <strong>Suzanne Brister</strong> is his latest. <strong>Lo Andrews</strong> is the guy he parties with later. Now, <strong>DDT</strong>, a.k.a., Dangerous Darrel Thomas (should'a been "Terrible Darrell Thompson", those journalists…*eye roll*), is another kinda pimp entirely. And a professional house sitter, lol. <strong>Charmin'</strong> are <strong>Melissa</strong> are some of his, um, ladies.<br /><br /><em>Part of Lucas' network</em><br /><strong>Susan Kelly</strong> is a dancer; <strong>Lori</strong> is her assistant. <strong>Ben Lincoln</strong> works at Ben's Darts &amp; Cues. <strong>Larry Hammet</strong> is at Trax Freight. <strong>Lannie Harrison</strong> is at Tulip's Hose Couplings and Fittings. <strong>Jan Murphy</strong> works at a sweatshop. <strong>Sandy Hue</strong> is at The Diamond Collective. <strong>Svege Tanner</strong> is at Strength and Beauty and finks on that jerk, <strong>Alex Truant</strong>. <strong>Coin</strong> is in the hospital and sober for the first time in decades. <strong>Elliot</strong> runs a metal-fabrication shop. <strong>Half-Moon Towing's owner</strong> is declaring bankruptcy. <strong>Gerry Haack</strong> was a lawn care guy who had some, um, problems. Now he's working at the Cobra Lounge, where it seems he still has some problems. <strong>Larry Lapp</strong> hangs at the Cobra; his wife, <strong>Marcella</strong>, would be really ticked off. <strong>Bob Brown</strong> deals in estate jewelry. <strong>Frank Stans</strong> is a bartender at the Bolo Lounge.<br /><br /><strong>The Cover and Title</strong><br />The cover is a blur of browns with an image of a woman's face. She's lying down, and if her face is anything to go by, she's screaming as a man's hands hold her in place. The author's name and the title are an embossed gold.<br /><br />The title is all about this killer's <em>Chosen Prey</em>. <br /></span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2421565984111956436"><br />“All extremes of feeling are allied with madness.”<br />? Virginia Woolf, Orlando<br /><br />Obsession.<br /><br />James Qatar is obsessed with small-town blond young women. But not because how they sparkle with life. Rather, it's how they look while dying being strangled by his favorite rope. As an art history professor and an intellectual, he has always been drawn to the beautiful deaths of asphyxiating women. Many many women.<br /><br />Blond Ellen Barstad is obsessed with sexual adventure. She thinks she has found the perfect teacher in Qatar. He certainly is interested in teaching her what she wants to know.<br /><br />Terry Marshall is obsessed with finding the killer of his blond niece. A deputy sheriff, he has compiled a file with facts about his niece's disappearance and included quite a few similar cases. Given the similarities of the disappearances, it looks like they've got a serial killer.<br /><br />Lucas Delaware has a new case.....<br /><br />And we have another great read in a series which is certain to obsess you.<br /><br /><br /></span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6421594576949980268">It has been two years since I read the previous book in the Prey series, but this was like hanging out with an old friend you haven't seen for a while - you fall back into old patterns like it was just yesterday. Another fast-paced search for a killer, another chilling glimpse into the killer's mind. I love the camaraderie between Davenport and his colleagues and chuckled out loud on many occasions. <br /><br />But the final sentence is a major cliffhanger! I do have the next book in the series on my bookshelf, but as I am a glutton for punishment I shall make myself wait a couple more months (at least!) before I read it, even though I am absolutely dying to know what happens!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12115978773500456478">Book 12 of Sandford's Lucas Davenport series.<br /><br />This book explores the demented mind of Professor James Qatar who is an art history professor at a small college in Minnesota. Qatar has a weird way of expressing his artistic side. He draws erotic photos of women...and then he kills them. As he has moved throughout the Midwest the bodies are left in his wake.<br /><br />Davenport and his support team are called to find the killer. Added to the team is an older police officer from Wisconsin who has let the hunt f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12115978773500456478">Book 12 of Sandford's Lucas Davenport series.<br /><br />This book explores the demented mind of Professor James Qatar who is an art history professor at a small college in Minnesota. Qatar has a weird way of expressing his artistic side. He draws erotic photos of women...and then he kills them. As he has moved throughout the Midwest the bodies are left in his wake.<br /><br />Davenport and his support team are called to find the killer. Added to the team is an older police officer from Wisconsin who has let the hunt for the killer get a little personal since his niece was one of the victims.<br /><br />Another good read about a demented killer. The only problem I had with the story was how Davenport figures out the killer is Qatar. That seemed a little farfetched to me. <br /><br />Some soft-core porn with Qatar and his current girlfriend. She was nearly as bizarre as he was. Seemed very eager to help catch Qatar which seemed odd since she was performing weird sex acts with him on a regular basis. She certainly didn't have much loyalty to her man.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3283773161540076426">This is another of the better books in John Sanford's "Prey" series (they're all good, so I suppose my differentiation is mostly because the characters in some grab me more than in others).   <span style="display:none" id="freeText3283773161540076426">This is another of the better books in John Sanford's "Prey" series (they're all good, so I suppose my differentiation is mostly because the characters in some grab me more than in others). But I <em>do</em> love it when the bad guy or gal - in this case a serial killer - is revealed to the reader up front. A big part of the thrill of the read, then, is how and when the identity will be known by the "hero" as well - in this case, Minneapolis Deputy Chief Lucas Davenport. Needless to say, there are zigs and zags along the way, interspersed with a look at the always evolving relationship with Davenport's friends and his now-fiance, Weather.<br /><br />As usual, Davenport figures it all out (albeit with a wicked twist or two), and also as usual, the book ends with a question that virtually guarantees readers will scramble to start the next one. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2411809375640148535">found this at a bus stop. i was almost finished with what i was reading at the time and as i did not have anything lined up for my next book i decided to try it. generally i avoid jumping into the middle of a series, especially a long-running one like this (didn't find out until i was half way through that this was number TWELVE O.o). i have stalled out on a number of series due to difficulties finding the next installment (book 2 of stephen hunter's bob lee swagger universe and book 5 of the GR</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2411809375640148535">found this at a bus stop. i was almost finished with what i was reading at the time and as i did not have anything lined up for my next book i decided to try it. generally i avoid jumping into the middle of a series, especially a long-running one like this (didn't find out until i was half way through that this was number TWELVE O.o). i have stalled out on a number of series due to difficulties finding the next installment (book 2 of stephen hunter's bob lee swagger universe and book 5 of the GRRM edited multi-writer series wild cards continue to elude me). i don't like feeling left out when characters reminisce over events in previous books (marcy and her gunshot wound). the story might be self-contained to each novel but the characters and the world they live in are not.<br /><br />as to this book itself, i thought it was alright until the third act. the incompetent bumblings of the police up against a man that no one would describe as a criminal "genius". and the ending seems to channel stephen king, specifically recent stephen king: set-up set-up set-up, cheap &amp; easy resolution, flaccid anti-climax. lucas could have talked the old man down, he could have physically stopped it, qatar could have attempted to escape and been shot, could have escaped successfully.... revenge isn't justice.<br /><br />i may or may not track down book 1 of this series and try to start from the beginning. i have not decided yet.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6121479949762666411">The bad guy in this 12th Prey book, is James Qatar, an art history professor and a repressed (although mild looking) psycho killer. He strangles his victims because that’s the only thing that pleasures him. At first a body of a young woman is discovered in a remote area, and the case is assigned to the local homicide team but when this site is suspected to be a graveyard where more murder victims are buried, Lucas Davenport and his team are tasked to find this serial killer. The investigation is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6121479949762666411">The bad guy in this 12th Prey book, is James Qatar, an art history professor and a repressed (although mild looking) psycho killer. He strangles his victims because that’s the only thing that pleasures him. At first a body of a young woman is discovered in a remote area, and the case is assigned to the local homicide team but when this site is suspected to be a graveyard where more murder victims are buried, Lucas Davenport and his team are tasked to find this serial killer. The investigation is quite interesting as Lucas is going from one clue to the next, slowly narrowing down the suspect pool. When another art professor and then the matron of a museum is killed, Lucas is sure he knows the killer is Qatar. (The museum curator was Qatar's mother, who had confronted him. Unfortunately Lucas and team don’t have enough evidence to proof it, yet.<br />Personally I thought the killer was very annoying; a weakling actually, and I didn’t like the pages dedicated to him. As always, I am most interesting in the investigation and the police procedural aspect. <br />The best thing about the Prey books is Lucas and the various personalities of the detectives in his team. Love their dynamics when they are on a case. ***3,5***</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2272732468498079760">I don't like Winter. (*nuff said)<br /><br />I listened to John Sanford's talk about this book a few days ago, and his process. I completely agree, if you want to critique a book, read it over and over, and figure out how they did what they did. He makes an observation that Lucas looks like a sexual preadtor with a number of women racking up as the books number increases. So its time to have him settle down.<br /><br /><br />Winter is using him like his first "baby's momma". Sandford's use of women in his series are pretty much all jaded and unless their biological clocks are ticking or their careers are put on back burner for awhile, lucas has no place with them.         <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer188128280">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11614016890324633579">This is the 12th in John Sandford's Prey series, and once again Lucas Davenport has a serial killer to catch. This is a good procedural in showing the day to day grunt work that goes into solving a crime of this sort. I read one review that complained that the end was obvious half way thru the story, and it was, but I think that was intentional. The end was just as obvious to Davenport as to the readers, and letting us in on the secret just showed that knowing the end does not mean we can do any</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11614016890324633579">This is the 12th in John Sandford's Prey series, and once again Lucas Davenport has a serial killer to catch. This is a good procedural in showing the day to day grunt work that goes into solving a crime of this sort. I read one review that complained that the end was obvious half way thru the story, and it was, but I think that was intentional. The end was just as obvious to Davenport as to the readers, and letting us in on the secret just showed that knowing the end does not mean we can do anything to change it. Thati s one of the realities most people never see in police work, and this book does a good job of letting the rest of us see the helplessness that comes with knowledge.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11614016890324633579">...more</a>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18420848244821461835">Chosen Prey (Lucas Davenport Book 12) Summary: He desired women: All kinds, all shapes, all sizes. He would fix on a woman and build imaginary stories around her. Some of the women he knew well, others not at all. Most of them faded quickly. Only a few became objects of desire. An art history professor and writer and cheerful pervert, James Qatar had a hobby: he took secret photographs of women and turned them into highly sexual drawings. One day, he took the hobby a step further and... well, one thing led to another, and he had to kill her. A man in his position couldn't be too careful, after all. And you know something? He LIKED it. Already faced with a welter of confusion in his personal life, Deputy Chief Lucas Davenport decides to take this case himself, hoping that some straightforward police work will clear his head, but as the trail begins to take some unexpected turns, it soon becomes clear that nothing is straightforward about this killer. The man is learning as he goes, Lucas realizes, taking great strides forward with each murder. He is becoming a monster - and Lucas may have no choice but to walk right into his lair.<br /><br />Rating: 3 1/2 stars<br /><br />Opening Line: "James Qatar dropped his feet over the edge of the bed and rubbed the back of his neck, a momentary veil of depression falling upon him."<br /><br />Quote: "We never looked in history."</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1046949200">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1046949200" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7809864-richard" class="left imgcol" title="Richard"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1329713377p2/7809864.jpg" alt="Richard" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1046949200?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 05, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7809864-richard" class="user" title="Richard">Richard</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7464584-chosen-prey" title="ebook 9780786526581" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1046949200">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16336679166508949161">This is another is the seemingly endless series of detective novels about Minnesota detective Lucas Davenport that features a villain who is a psychopathic serial killer who preys on women. One might believe that all the psychos in the country live in Minnesota. Perhaps I have read too many of the author's novels, but this is getting stale. I believe there are other kinds of criminals to be written about, and stories about tracking and capturing them might be interesting.<br /><br />I like a detective hero</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16336679166508949161">This is another is the seemingly endless series of detective novels about Minnesota detective Lucas Davenport that features a villain who is a psychopathic serial killer who preys on women. One might believe that all the psychos in the country live in Minnesota. Perhaps I have read too many of the author's novels, but this is getting stale. I believe there are other kinds of criminals to be written about, and stories about tracking and capturing them might be interesting.<br /><br />I like a detective hero who is smart. Usually, the author presents his protagonist, Lucas Davenport, as a shrewd and smart detective. Not this time. After identifying the serial killer, a man who has murdered more than ten people, Davenport has him tailed loosely, with only a single detective assigned to follow and watch him. Naturally, the killer easily evades the single detective and goes on to murder again. This nothing short of MORONIC on the part of the lead detective. What real cop would ever be so careless? <br /><br />The story drags quite a bit. There isn't much suspense, and there is little action. Ho hum. Skip this one.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16336679166508949161">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_918402032">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/918402032" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/15166873-paula-dembeck" class="left imgcol" title="Paula Dembeck"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Paula Dembeck" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/918402032?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 23, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15166873-paula-dembeck" class="user" title="Paula Dembeck">Paula Dembeck</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer918402032">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15101384673047091630">Number 12 in the ongoing Prey Series.<br /><br />This hunt for a serial killer is one that reminds us all that some of the nastiest killers are wolves dressed in sheep’s clothing. James Qatar has a credible veneer as an art history professor at St Patrick’s University and as a writer with a publishing record. He is also a thief and a killer. He loves good clothes (cashmere, fine tailored suits and driving gloves) and good wine and when he has the cash, he loves to shop at SAKS and Neiman Marcus. He also lik</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15101384673047091630">Number 12 in the ongoing Prey Series.<br /><br />This hunt for a serial killer is one that reminds us all that some of the nastiest killers are wolves dressed in sheep’s clothing. James Qatar has a credible veneer as an art history professor at St Patrick’s University and as a writer with a publishing record. He is also a thief and a killer. He loves good clothes (cashmere, fine tailored suits and driving gloves) and good wine and when he has the cash, he loves to shop at SAKS and Neiman Marcus. He also likes women of a particular shape and size, specifically blonde petite woman who he romances and then kills.<br /><br />Qatar has an interesting methodology, secretly photographing women and then working with his digital camera, art and computers programs to photoshop the results. By lifting photos from one image to another, he grafts the bodies from women on a porno site to the heads of the women he has surreptitiously photographed. He then fixes on and builds imaginary stories around her and mails the pictures to his victims, secretly pleasured to think of their response as they open their mail. <br /><br />James is intelligent and so organized that the police do not suspect him or even know of his existence. But now the wind may have shifted and Qatar’s secret life may have started to unravel. The arrival of spring has unearthed the body of a young woman who has been dead about a year. The initial investigation reveals she did not frequent bars and was not involved in drugs. She was just a girl working as a waitress in a restaurant in St Paul who did freelance work in the art community designing ads and websites. The police are puzzled. And now women are beginning to come forward with pornographic drawings mailed to them anonymously. And then another drawing is found posted in a public place….<br /><br />Lucas recruits his former team and begins the investigation. Marcy Sherrill, on medical leave and still recovering from her bullet wounds from a previous story, is brought in to coordinate. As publicity about the murder blankets the TV stations, deputy sheriff Terry Marshall arrives from Wisconsin. He has been searching for his missing niece Laura for nine years and he feels the profile of the murders may be similar to that of his niece. He is desperate to help.<br /><br />Lucas and Weather are together once more. They had once been headed for marriage but that was derailed when Weather was taken hostage by a crazy biker in a case Lucas worked on. There was a violent bloody ambush and the biker was killed, but Weather, caught in the middle was traumatized by the experience and it has taken her some time to recover. Now, after being apart for a couple of years they have made their way back to one another. At the age of thirty nine, Weather’s baby alarm is ringing and she is ready to have a child. So the ring comes out of the drawer and marriage is once more on the table.<br /><br />In the background, there are stirrings of potential changes at city hall. The mayor has decided not to run for re-election and so political appointees Chief Rose Marie and Deputy Chief Lucas, may both be without jobs. <br /><br />The murderer this time is not the usual nasty villain of Sanford’s past books. He is an annoying, repulsive and obsessive wimp, who even cries as he complains about not being understood. He is smart though and very careful about leaving incriminating evidence. We know some of his background but it would have been interesting to hear more of his childhood and upbringing to appreciate his spiral into darkness. <br /><br />This is definitely better than the last Prey novel which I found very disappointing. The Sanford I knew appears to be back. However I did not sense any of the growing caring connection between Weather and Lucas from the previous books and there have also been a few unexplained leaps: the fling with Marcy simply seems to have come to a natural death. Fine, but what ever happened to Catrin, the old college girlfriend that was divorcing her husband? She and Lucas had met up and something seemed to be brewing. Where did that go?<br /><br />However the other characters and the relationships between them do continue to grow and develop and Lucas’s life does move forward. He is now concerned about renovating the house for a potential family and less concerned about bedding the next cute skirt that passes by. Several books ago when we first met Lucas he was a bit over the top (the part I liked about him!) but now he seems much more settled and thoughtful. <br /><br />I found this adventure was more focused on the crime and less on Lucas’s thoughts and personal life. In this one we know who the killer is, the suspense comes from watching him try to crack the case and not knowing whether the murderer can be brought to justice or will simply walk away. In the end there are always questions about how Lucas handled a case. We still see and feel that sense of Lucas going rogue, interested more in justice than the rules of the game.<br /><br />The ending creates some interesting speculation for the next book, which I will read now that I have been reassured that Sanford is back in his game. This is not as good as some of his others but definitely better than the last read.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15101384673047091630">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/2509211-jim" class="user" title="Jim">Jim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer345591062">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15744135139698369532">Another great detective story by John Sandford. This story has the Assistant Chief of Police Lucas Davenport trying to figure out what and to who are strange murders happening. Obviously a mass murderer but who and why as each murder scene is totally cleaned by the criminal. Watching and experiencing the clue seeking and detective work of Lucas are spell binding and just plain hard to put down detective whodunit mystery work. I have come to really enjoy all of Sandford's writings. A must read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer350222314">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11444873503225517153">This time the serial killer is art history professor James Qatar. He is fixated on young blondes.<br /><br />This is a great Prey book. The reader knows the killer and gets to watch as Lucas Davenport and his team stumble their way through the clues.<br /><br />Davenport is back with Weather and a marriage is being planned and maybe even a child. Davenport seems to have settled down somewhat and even grown up a bit.<br /><br />Loved the book and the development of the characters </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/753098367?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 06, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1185451-sandi" class="user" title="Sandi">Sandi</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer14391308206359790166">Usually I try to avoid books with serial killer plots but this series has always been the exception. For whatever reason I always enjoy reading about Lucas and his cohorts. This entry hints at some big changes both professionally and personally for Lucas which makes me eager to read the next book in the series. Listened to the audio which was read by <strong>Richard Ferrone</strong>. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1211062685">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1211062685" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/22271857-truman32" class="left imgcol" title="Truman32"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1375371520p2/22271857.jpg" alt="Truman32" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1211062685?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/22271857-truman32" class="user" title="Truman32">Truman32</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1211062685">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5318594690417086235"><br /><strong>Chosen Prey</strong> is John Sandford’s 12th Lucas Davenport novel and it’s clear that here at the mid-point of this series he is just hitting his stride. The writing is sharp, the action crisp, and the killer appropriately disturbing. <br /><br />Not surprisingly, there’s another killer loose in Minneapolis, and it is up to Deputy Police Chief Davenport and his crew of stalwart and dedicated police to catch him. James Qatar is a professor of art history by day, but out of the classroom he is hiding something. What</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5318594690417086235"><br /><strong>Chosen Prey</strong> is John Sandford’s 12th Lucas Davenport novel and it’s clear that here at the mid-point of this series he is just hitting his stride. The writing is sharp, the action crisp, and the killer appropriately disturbing. <br /><br />Not surprisingly, there’s another killer loose in Minneapolis, and it is up to Deputy Police Chief Davenport and his crew of stalwart and dedicated police to catch him. James Qatar is a professor of art history by day, but out of the classroom he is hiding something. What could it be? A beanie baby habit? An addiction to fried food? Ambitions of being the best Elvis impersonator in the Minneapolis area? Unfortunately, no. He’s a deranged killer that has an voracious compulsion to seduce young inexperienced women from small towns and rural areas, engage them in bizarre sex and then kill them. Qatar has all kinds of issues going on, starting with his relationship with his mother and ending with the strong appetite to strangle young blonde women. The worms in his brain propagate in a cesspool of freakish notions and abnormal aspirations. <br /><br />Qatar comes off at first as a kind of sad, foolish, balding man—someone to be pitied. But his murderous impulses and the wreckage he leaves in his wake detailed in a chilling chapter with the discovery of a secret mass graveyard spell out how depraved and horrible this man truly is.<br /><br />The gang is all here for the hunt: Marcy Sherrill (recovering from the gunshot wounds taken in the previous book), Sloan, Del, and Weather; and the story unfolds in a reliably exciting manner.<br /><br />What I really enjoy about Sandford’s Prey novels is the light it shines on the everyday workings of the Minneapolis police force. Like the television show, ER, these novels celebrate the working man. They show the everyday laborer—in this case members of a police force—as they struggle to do their job in a thorough and first rate manner. There are moments of indecision, wrong choices made, good-natured banter with co-workers, and lots of hard work. I love the idea that the detective investigating a crime does not have to be haunted or driven by ghosts, but only wants to do his job well, and that is enough to succeed.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5318594690417086235">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13356716071951070866">*** Contains some spoilers!<br /><br />Let me preface this by saying, I enjoy John Sandford novels. Some are better than others, but they are still fun reads. Chosen Prey was an extremely fun novel. It begins with an Art History Professor who has a lust for killing. Sprinkle it with some snail mailed bizarre art work. Add some new characters who you hope stay around for another book, but you know deep down that they are doomed to die. Finally get Lucas in his Porsche speeding to crime scene after crime scene. That is the recipe for a book you look forward to completing.<br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_974376800">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/974376800" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/31620959-lena" class="left imgcol" title="Lena"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1400785820p2/31620959.jpg" alt="Lena" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/974376800?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 11, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/31620959-lena" class="user" title="Lena">Lena</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer974376800">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14189963557338055092">Couldn’t hold a candle to the previous Prey books<br /><br />I read the first eleven books and regard myself as a Prey Series fan. All of them are very well written with intelligent plots constructed around rich characters, which made me enjoy the reading and kept me interested throughout the page-turning, riveting and surprising stories. In all previous books both Davenport and the killer enthralled me: the detective’s line of thoughts, the way he undertakes the chases, the turns in the events, the suspens</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14189963557338055092">Couldn’t hold a candle to the previous Prey books<br /><br />I read the first eleven books and regard myself as a Prey Series fan. All of them are very well written with intelligent plots constructed around rich characters, which made me enjoy the reading and kept me interested throughout the page-turning, riveting and surprising stories. In all previous books both Davenport and the killer enthralled me: the detective’s line of thoughts, the way he undertakes the chases, the turns in the events, the suspenseful way things unfold, everything always masterfully taken care of. <br />Chosen Prey is a readable and relatively enjoyable book but, in my opinion, it doesn’t challenge people’s curiosity and interest as much as the others do. The plot is weak and the end is predictable from the very beginning of the story, which evolves through feeble and obvious dialogues. Davenport’s great skills are there, at the service of finding the killer, but in a way that did not bring me along throughout his conclusions as he always does.<br />We know who the criminal is from the first chapter, so it is not a whodunit story, not a bad thing in itself at all, but one in which Davenport has to follow clues to get closer, further, then closer again, until he solves the mystery. For me, in this book, this movement happens in a slightly tedious way, through too many drug related characters with confused and meaningless connections with the criminal, something that creates a subplot that seems too artificial.<br />The killer, Qatar, is an uninteresting, inconsistent, and undeveloped character, with erratic and sheer mean actions, whose psyche we do not get to know enough so that his behavior can make any sense, even if it is a sick one. I think the character’s lack of density makes it unlikely to bring on in the reader any kind of fruitful feeling. <br /> To put it in a nutshell, I think the author lost his gripping in this book. However, as I regard him as one of the best authors of mystery/thrillers, the experience with Chosen Prey has not discouraged me to keep reading the series nor should my review do so to those who like the genre. I just really hope that he brings back his qualified and brilliant style from the next volume on.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14189963557338055092">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_401586298">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/401586298" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/892406-kristin" class="left imgcol" title="Kristin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1387900363p2/892406.jpg" alt="Kristin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/401586298?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 15, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/892406-kristin" class="user" title="Kristin">Kristin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/892406-kristin?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/892406-kristin?shelf=audio-books" class="actionLinkLite">audio-books</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer401586298">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6641218712085306191">Alas, we went back to the format of knowing what the psychotic killer is thinking and doing since book #11. And yes, the guy is a scumbag of the worst kind. Not even a bad buy the reader can emphasize with. You want him caught, and you want him caught now. <br /><br /><br />The downside to Chosen Prey is our killer seems to be one step ahead of the police. I've noticed this pattern in previous books: something alerts the killer by accident that the police might be looking for him, the murderer does a few things t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6641218712085306191">Alas, we went back to the format of knowing what the psychotic killer is thinking and doing since book #11. And yes, the guy is a scumbag of the worst kind. Not even a bad buy the reader can emphasize with. You want him caught, and you want him caught now. <br /><br /><br />The downside to Chosen Prey is our killer seems to be one step ahead of the police. I've noticed this pattern in previous books: something alerts the killer by accident that the police might be looking for him, the murderer does a few things to hide evidence, the police actually meet the psychopath but only the creep knows it, then ah ha! Davenport has a strong hunch he knows who done it and puts a tail on our perp. But guess what! Yes! The perp figures out he's being tailed and slips the net! Oh no! <br /><br /><br />And so on and so forth till we come to our Big Dramatic Conclusion, or in this case, Big Let Down because I saw the ending(s) coming much like a severe thunderstorm sports tornadoes on the prairie during July. <br /><br /><br />The one other item that distracted me a bit was we've moved forward a solid year since book 11: where Davenport had a college friend wanting to get in his pants, was screwing a potter, and had his ex-fiance making noises like she wanted to get back together. Book 11 left off on a bit of a cliff hanger, which was not really picked up here because we find that Weather has overcome all of her issues and is now talking baby. Whaa? It felt like a lot was just kinda skipped to move the Weather/Davenport personal issues forward. <br /><br /><br />Not one of my favorites because the plot and characters were so transparent to me in this book. <br /></span>

          </span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90506136" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3305776-joe" class="left imgcol" title="Joe"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1382233276p2/3305776.jpg" alt="Joe" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/90506136?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 21, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3305776-joe" class="user" title="Joe">Joe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3305776-joe?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer90506136">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4982515086180459164">Here we go again. This one has my favorite ending yet. The often present suspicion hanging around Lucas at the end of a case, is masterfully handled. While Lucas is assuaging his conscience, his peers hold the hush, information leaks strategically to the press, and politicians praise the department for the way the case was handled although everybody knows something wasn't quite right.<br />Mission accomplished. Justice served.<br /><br />Once again... beautiful.<br /><br />Think about it. Sandford doesn't start out with anyt</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4982515086180459164">Here we go again. This one has my favorite ending yet. The often present suspicion hanging around Lucas at the end of a case, is masterfully handled. While Lucas is assuaging his conscience, his peers hold the hush, information leaks strategically to the press, and politicians praise the department for the way the case was handled although everybody knows something wasn't quite right.<br />Mission accomplished. Justice served.<br /><br />Once again... beautiful.<br /><br />Think about it. Sandford doesn't start out with anything new. A serial murder and an investigation. Lots of people write that. Sanford just writes it well. He is a master of leading and feeding the mind of the reader. He leaves no stone unturned, no twist unraveled, and no question unanswered. Timing is flawless. The balance between plots and between characters, perfect.<br /><br />This time we get the subtle, strong character of out of town Deputy Terry Marshall tagging along, stepping up when the heat is on, and stepping in to flip steaks on the barbee. Marshall is obscurely and perfectly developed for his supporting role here. Lucas and Del never give an opinion of Marshall. They more than tolerate him accompanying them on the case, but Sandford leaves it to the reader to form the opinion. Then we get Weather’s opinion at the exact perfect time.<br /><br />There aren't words strong enough to describe the quality of John Sandford's writing. If you find a 'weakness', it is there deliberately. If you find a hole... Forget it! You're not gonna find a hole! Sandford could write Lucas Davenport all the way into the nursing home and it will be a blast! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4982515086180459164">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8amG8sFwqJanTVUJzAMPObWShfNatli5EdUUv6pb11yUfbkhM6K8bCuVIbKyYumL/GVG6hNrHxN73BEtZs4hGQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0gpfxUEd21HEkU3jEYqSY8/gDNs+6fkezI4qGhTOfhK33mAWs8/Pq0hJOVhv63TRhhfPwnc0vrSmhy+I2FuIVw==')})
  }

Rhyme agrees to find the boy while awaiting his operation. But even Rhyme can\'t anticipate that Sachs will disagree with his crime analysis and that her vehemence will put her in the swampland, harboring the very suspect whom Rhyme considers a ruthless killer.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4610.John_Sandford">About John Sandford</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/4610.John_Sandford"><img alt="4610" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1202524015p2/4610.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer5126786831915352626">John Sandford was born John Camp on February 23, 1944, in Cedar Rapids, Iowa. He attended the public schools in Cedar Rapids, graduating from Washington High School in 1962. He then spent four years at the University of Iowa, graduating with a bachelor's degree in American Studies in 1966. In 1966, he married Susan Lee Jones of Cedar Rapids, a fellow student at the University of Iowa. He was in th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5126786831915352626">John Sandford was born John Camp on February 23, 1944, in Cedar Rapids, Iowa. He attended the public schools in Cedar Rapids, graduating from Washington High School in 1962. He then spent four years at the University of Iowa, graduating with a bachelor's degree in American Studies in 1966. In 1966, he married Susan Lee Jones of Cedar Rapids, a fellow student at the University of Iowa. He was in the U.S. Army from 1966-68, worked as a reporter for the Cape Girardeau Southeast Missourian from 1968-1970, and went back to the University of Iowa from 1970-1971, where he received a master's degree in journalism. He was a reporter for The Miami Herald from 1971-78, and then a reporter for the St. Paul Pioneer-Press from 1978-1990; in 1980, he was a finalist for a Pulitzer Prize, and he won the Pulitzer in 1986 for a series of stories about a midwestern farm crisis. From 1990 to the present he has written thriller novels. He's also the author of two non-fiction books, one on plastic surgery and one on art. He is the principal financial backer of a major archeological project in the Jordan Valley of Israel, with a website at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.rehov.org" target="_blank">www.rehov.org</a> In addition to archaeology, he is deeply interested in art (painting) and photography. He both hunts and fishes. He has two children, Roswell and Emily, and one grandson, Benjamin. His wife, Susan, died of metastasized breast cancer in May, 2007, and is greatly missed.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5126786831915352626">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/4610.John_Sandford" class="actionLink moreLink">More about John Sandford...</a>
